said Jensen Huang, founder and CEO of NVIDIA. &#8220;Compute demand keeps accelerating and compounding across training and inference &#8212; each growing exponentially. We&#8217;ve entered the virtuous cycle of AI. The AI ecosystem is scaling fast &#8212; with more new foundation model makers, more AI startups, across more industries, and in more countries. AI is going everywhere, doing everything, all at once.&#8221;</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">During the first nine months of fiscal 2026, NVIDIA returned $37.0 billion to shareholders in the form of shares repurchased and cash dividends. These non-GAAP measures include non-GAAP gross profit, non-GAAP gross margin, non-GAAP operating expenses, non-GAAP operating income, non-GAAP other income (expense), net, non-GAAP net income, non-GAAP net income, or earnings, per diluted share, and free cash flow. For NVIDIA&#8217;s investors to be better able to compare its current results with those of previous periods, the company has shown a reconciliation of GAAP to non-GAAP financial measures. These reconciliations adjust the related GAAP financial measures to exclude stock-based compensation expense, acquisition-related and other costs, other, gains&#47;losses from non-marketable and publicly-held equity securities, net, interest expense related to amortization of debt discount, and the associated tax impact of these items where applicable. Free cash flow is calculated as GAAP net cash provided by operating activities less both purchases related to property and equipment and intangible assets and principal payments on property and equipment and intangible assets. NVIDIA believes the presentation of its non-GAAP financial measures enhances the user&#8217;s overall understanding of the company&#8217;s historical financial performance. The presentation of the company&#8217;s non-GAAP financial measures is not meant to be considered in isolation or as a substitute for the company&#8217;s financial results prepared in accordance with GAAP, and the company&#8217;s non-GAAP measures may be different from non-GAAP measures used by other companies.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font 1pt 2px 0;text-align:right;vertical-align:middle"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:10pt;font-weight:400;line-height:100%">%</font></td></tr></table></div><div style="margin-bottom:12pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">We specialize in markets where our computing platforms can provide tremendous acceleration for applications. These platforms incorporate processors, interconnects, software, algorithms, systems, and services to deliver unique value. Our platforms address four large markets where our expertise is critical&#58; Data Center, Gaming, Professional Visualization, and Automotive.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt"><font style="color:#76b900;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Revenue</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Revenue for the third quarter was a record $57.0 billion, up 62% from a year ago and up 22% sequentially. </font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Data Center revenue for the third quarter was a record $51.2 billion, up 66% from a year ago and up 25% sequentially, driven by three platform shifts - accelerated computing, powerful AI models, and agentic applications. Blackwell Ultra is now our leading architecture across all customer categories while our prior Blackwell architecture saw continued strong demand. H20 sales were insignificant in the third quarter.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Data Center compute revenue was a record $43.0 billion, up 56% from a year ago and up 27% sequentially. Networking revenue was a record $8.2 billion, up 162% from a year ago from the introduction and continued growth of NVLink compute fabric for GB200 and GB300 systems. Networking revenue was up 13% sequentially, driven by the growth of XDR InfiniBand products, NVLink&#8482;, and Ethernet for AI solutions, while shipment timing and supply availability varied compared to the prior quarter. </font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Gaming revenue for the third quarter was up 30% from a year ago on the continued demand for Blackwell. Gaming revenue was down 1% sequentially as channel inventories have reached more normalized levels heading into the holiday season.  </font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Professional Visualization revenue for the third quarter was up 56% from a year ago and up 26% sequentially, driven by the launch of our new DGX Spark&#8482; as well as the growth of Blackwell sales.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:12pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Automotive revenue for the third quarter was up 32% from a year ago and up 1% sequentially, driven by continued adoption of our self-driving platforms.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt"><font style="color:#76b900;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Gross Margin</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:12pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">GAAP and non-GAAP gross margins for the third quarter decreased from a year ago as our business model transitioned from offering Hopper HGX&#8482; systems to Blackwell full-scale datacenter solutions. As expected, our GAAP and non-GAAP gross margins increased sequentially as Blackwell ramped with an improved mix and cost structure.</font></div><div style="height:42.75pt;position:relative;width:100%"><div style="bottom:0;position:absolute;width:100%"><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font><br></font></div></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><div style="min-height:42.75pt;width:100%"><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font><br></font></div></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt"><font style="color:#76b900;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Expenses</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:12pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">GAAP operating expenses for the third quarter were up 36% from a year ago and up 8% sequentially, and non-GAAP operating expenses were up 38% from a year ago and up 11% sequentially. The increases were primarily driven by compute and infrastructure costs, higher compensation and benefits due to compensation increases and employee growth and engineering development costs for new product introductions.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt"><font style="color:#76b900;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Other Income &#38; Expense and Income Tax</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">GAAP other income and expense (OI&#38;E) includes interest income, interest expense, and non-marketable and publicly-held equity securities gains or losses. Non-GAAP OI&#38;E excludes non-marketable and publicly-held equity securities gains or losses.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Interest income for the third quarter was $624 million, up from a year ago and sequentially, reflecting growth in cash, cash equivalents, and debt securities. Net other income for the third quarter was $1.4 billion, primarily driven by gains in non-marketable and publicly-held equity securities. </font></div><div style="margin-bottom:12pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">GAAP effective tax rate for the third quarter was 15.9%, an increase from a year ago reflecting a lower percentage of tax benefits from stock-based compensation and U.S. federal research tax credit relative to the increase in income before income tax. Non-GAAP effective tax rate for the third quarter was 17.1%.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt"><font style="color:#76b900;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Balance Sheet and Cash Flow</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Cash, cash equivalents and marketable securities were $60.6 billion, up from $38.5 billion a year ago and $56.8 billion a quarter ago. The increases primarily reflect higher revenue, partially offset by stock repurchases.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Accounts receivable was $33.4 billion with 53 days sales outstanding (DSO), down from 54 days sequentially, driven by timing of cash collections.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Inventory was $19.8 billion, up from $15.0 billion sequentially, and total supply-related commitments were $50.3 billion. We are ordering to secure long lead-time components, meet the demand for Blackwell, and support future architecture ramps.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Multi-year cloud service agreements were $26.0 billion, up from $12.6 billion sequentially, to support our research and development efforts and DGX&#8482; Cloud offerings.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Cash flow from operating activities was $23.8 billion, up from $17.6 billion a year ago and up from $15.4 billion a quarter ago. The year-on-year and sequential increases reflect growth in revenue.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:12pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">We returned $12.7 billion to shareholders in the third quarter through $12.5 billion of share repurchases and $243 million of cash dividends.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt"><font style="color:#76b900;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Fourth Quarter of Fiscal 2026 Outlook</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA style="color:#76b900;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:700;line-height:120%;text-decoration:underline">Non-GAAP Measures</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:11pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">To supplement NVIDIA&#8217;s condensed consolidated financial statements presented in accordance with GAAP, the company uses non-GAAP measures of certain components of financial performance. These non-GAAP measures include non-GAAP gross profit, non-GAAP gross margin, non-GAAP operating expenses, non-GAAP operating income, non-GAAP other income (expense), net, non-GAAP net income, non-GAAP net income, or earnings, per diluted share, and free cash flow. For NVIDIA&#8217;s investors to be better able to compare its current results with those of previous periods, the company has shown a reconciliation of GAAP to non-GAAP financial measures. These reconciliations adjust the related GAAP financial measures to exclude stock-based compensation expense, acquisition-related and other costs, other, gains&#47;losses from non-marketable and publicly-held equity securities, net, interest expense related to amortization of debt discount, and the associated tax impact of these items where applicable. Free cash flow is calculated as GAAP net cash provided by operating activities less both purchases related to property and equipment and intangible assets and principal payments on property and equipment and intangible assets. NVIDIA believes the presentation of its non-GAAP financial measures enhances the user's overall understanding of the company&#8217;s historical financial performance. The presentation of the company&#8217;s non-GAAP financial measures is not meant to be considered in isolation or as a substitute for the company&#8217;s financial results prepared in accordance with GAAP, and the company&#8217;s non-GAAP measures may be different from non-GAAP measures used by other companies.</font></div><div style="margin-bottom:9pt;text-align:justify"><font style="color:#000000;font-family:'NVIDIA Sans',sans-serif;font-size:9pt;font-weight:400;line-height:120%">Certain statements in this CFO Commentary including, but not limited to, statements as to&#58; expectations with respect to growth, performance and benefits of our products, services, and technologies, including Blackwell, and related trends and drivers&#59; expectations with respect to supply and demand for our products, services, and technologies, including Blackwell, and related matters including inventory, production and distribution&#59; expectations with respect to NVIDIA&#8217;s third party arrangements, including with its collaborators and partners&#59; expectations with respect to technology developments and related trends and drivers&#59; our financial and business outlook for the fourth quarter of fiscal 2026 and beyond&#59; projected market growth and trends&#59; expectations with respect to AI and related industries&#59; and other statements that are not historical facts are forward-looking statements within the meaning of Section 27A of the Securities Act of 1933, as amended, and Section 21E of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended, which are subject to the &#8220;safe harbor&#8221; created by those sections based on management&#8217;s beliefs and assumptions and on information currently available to management and are subject to risks and uncertainties that could cause results to be materially different than expectations.
